752729164856805_752744988188556	10204145836358105	Okay so this is a very wrongly presented information by The Logical Indian. The first thing we need to know the bill is not incorrect by any means. Let's come to the legal part. Service tax is applicable on food items which are sold in an AC restaurant. It is calculated as 40% of total bill ( gross amount + service charges)Coming to the service charge part, they are mandatory if mentioned on the menu. If not you can very well refute it but if they have mentioned on menu and you are not satisfied with the service you have to pay them. Yes, service charge is a type of tip you give to the restaurant but it's upon restaurants to charge it or not.Considering the VAT part it is different for different states. Talking specifically about Delhi VAT on food items is 12.5% and on Drinks (alcoholic and aerated) is 20%. Vat can't be applied on packaged products which are being sold on MRP, i.e. no value addition is done by restaurant in it. Vat, unlike service tax is applicable on whole of bill amount but that again only in AC restaurants.So summing it all up a typical bill shouldn't exceed 30-33% extra amount on gross amount.Thus first of all make sure service charge is NOT ILLEGAL as 'portrayed' in the above post.Now coming to the part of such huge amount of taxes being collected. Well, it was us who chose our government by means of casting votes and if you dig deep into the tax system you won't be able to get out of it without a crocin tablet. 752729164856805_752766158186439	10155864560015341	As a hotelier, let me clarify that the Service Tax authorities do not give clear advise on whether to charge Service Tax on food served in Restaurants in a hotel. This is what the rule states : "restaurant having the facility of air conditioned or central air heating in any part of the establishment at any time during the years" . So, I assume that if a restaurant in a hotel isn't going to file its taxes as a separate entity (having a separate PAN, TAN, TIN and ST registration number) , then the air conditioned rooms in the hotel (lodging section) will make the restaurant liable to collect Service Tax. It is better for the Hotel to err on the side of caution and collect more money and deposit it to the government rather than have the authorities come and say that we've collected lesser and then have us pay the differential amount (which can run into lakhs) along with interest and penalties. If the restaurant is a separate entity, then the hotel ceases to be a hotel. It becomes a lodge. So even a restaurant WITHOUT air conditioning will charge you Service Tax if it has air conditioned even a manager's room.It is very easy to feel outraged about how restaurants are overcharging. But I request all of you to see the troubles the restaurants are facing before commenting about how restaurants or hotels are cheats.P.S., Regarding Service Charge, it is the only way the staff (who are in dangerously low in availability) are kept satisfied. There is NO LAW barring the levy of a Service Charge by the establishment. It is actually levied by restaraunts at their discretion as a gratuity and is done at the outlets discretion. "Service Charge is not a tax, never has been" but it is a charge that covers tips , staff welfare & other misc stuff like breakages etc.   .      .
